<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en"><i>Hamilton</i> (musical)</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p><i><b>Hamilton: An American Musical</b></i> is a <a href="/wiki/Sung-through" title="Sung-through">sung- and rapped-through</a> musical about the life of <a href="/wiki/Founding_Fathers_of_the_United_States" title="Founding Fathers of the United States">American Founding Father</a> <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton" title="Alexander Hamilton">Alexander Hamilton</a>, with music, lyrics and book by <a href="/wiki/Lin-Manuel_Miranda" title="Lin-Manuel Miranda">Lin-Manuel Miranda</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brantley_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-brantley-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Donaldson_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Donaldson-2">[2]</a></sup> inspired by the 2004 biography <a href="/wiki/Ron_Chernow#Alexander_Hamilton" title="Ron Chernow"><i>Alexander Hamilton</i></a> by historian <a href="/wiki/Ron_Chernow" title="Ron Chernow">Ron Chernow</a>. Notably incorporating <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip-hop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">rhythm and blues</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Show_tune" title="Show tune">traditional-style show tunes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Color-blind_casting" title="Color-blind casting">color-conscious casting</a> of non-white actors as the Founding Fathers and other historical figures,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cote_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cote-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mead_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-mead-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atlantic_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-atlantic-5">[5]</a></sup> the musical achieved both critical acclaim and box office success.</p>
<p>The musical made its <a href="/wiki/Off-Broadway" title="Off-Broadway">Off-Broadway</a> debut at <a href="/wiki/The_Public_Theater" title="The Public Theater">The Public Theater</a> in February 2015, where its engagement was sold out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Revolutionary_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Revolutionary-6">[6]</a></sup> The show transferred to <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a> in August 2015 at the <a href="/wiki/Richard_Rodgers_Theatre" title="Richard Rodgers Theatre">Richard Rodgers Theatre</a>. On Broadway, it received enthusiastic critical reception and unprecedented advance box office sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoxOffice1_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-BoxOffice1-7">[7]</a></sup> In 2016, <i>Hamilton</i> received a record-setting 16 <a href="/wiki/70th_Tony_Awards" title="70th Tony Awards">Tony</a> nominations, winning 11, including <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Musical">Best Musical</a>, and was also the recipient of the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Musical_Theater_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Musical Theater Album">Grammy Award for Best Musical Theater Album</a> and the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_Drama" title="Pulitzer Prize for Drama">Pulitzer Prize for Drama</a>. The prior off-Broadway production of <i>Hamilton</i> won the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Drama_Desk_Award_for_Outstanding_Musical" title="Drama Desk Award for Outstanding Musical">Drama Desk Award for Outstanding Musical</a> as well as seven other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drama_Desk_Awards" title="Drama Desk Awards">Drama Desk Awards</a> out of 14 total nominated categories.</p>
<p>The Chicago production of <i>Hamilton</i> began preview performances at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PrivateBank_Theatre" title="PrivateBank Theatre">PrivateBank Theatre</a> in September 2016 and officially opened the following month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chicago_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-chicago-8">[8]</a></sup> The first U.S. national tour of the show began performances in March 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> A production of <i>Hamilton</i> will open in the <a href="/wiki/West_End_theatre" title="West End theatre">West End</a> in December 2017 at the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Palace_Theatre" title="Victoria Palace Theatre">Victoria Palace Theatre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-10">[10]</a></sup> A second U.S. tour is also set to begin performances in early 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Desk_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Desk-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>On February 14, 2017, Miranda confirmed that a film adaptation based on the musical is in the works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Synopsis">Synopsis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Synopsis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Act_One">Act One</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Act One">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The musical begins with the company summarizing <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton" title="Alexander Hamilton">Alexander Hamilton</a>'s early life as an orphan in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> ("<a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton_(song)" title="Alexander Hamilton (song)">Alexander Hamilton</a>"). Hamilton was born out of wedlock in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>—his father abandoned him at an early age and his mother died when Hamilton was twelve. By nineteen, Hamilton has made his way to the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">American colonies</a>, a dedicated supporter of <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American independence</a>.</p>
<p>In the summer of 1776 in New York City, Hamilton seeks out <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Burr" title="Aaron Burr">Aaron Burr</a>. Burr advises the overenthusiastic Hamilton to "talk less; smile more". Hamilton is unable to understand why Burr would rather exercise caution than fight for his beliefs ("Aaron Burr, Sir"). Hamilton bonds with three fellow revolutionaries: abolitionist <a href="/wiki/John_Laurens" title="John Laurens">John Laurens</a>, the flamboyant Frenchman <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_du_Motier,_Marquis_de_Lafayette" title="Gilbert du Motier, Marquis de Lafayette">Marquis de Lafayette</a>, and the tailor's apprentice <a href="/wiki/Hercules_Mulligan" title="Hercules Mulligan">Hercules Mulligan</a>. Hamilton dazzles them with his rhetorical skills ("<a href="/wiki/My_Shot" title="My Shot">My Shot</a>") and they dream of laying down their lives for their cause ("<a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_Tonight" title="The Story of Tonight">The Story of Tonight</a>"). Meanwhile, the wealthy Schuyler sisters—<a href="/wiki/Angelica_Schuyler_Church" title="Angelica Schuyler Church">Angelica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Schuyler_Hamilton" title="Elizabeth Schuyler Hamilton">Eliza</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peggy_Schuyler" title="Peggy Schuyler">Peggy</a>—wander the streets of New York, excited by the spirit of revolution in the air ("<a href="/wiki/The_Schuyler_Sisters" title="The Schuyler Sisters">The Schuyler Sisters</a>").</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samuel_Seabury_(bishop)" title="Samuel Seabury (bishop)">Samuel Seabury</a>, a vocal <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">Loyalist</a>, preaches against the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, and Hamilton <a href="/wiki/The_Farmer_Refuted" title="The Farmer Refuted">refutes and ridicules his statements</a> ("Farmer Refuted"). A message arrives from <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George III of the United Kingdom">King George III</a>, reminding the colonists that he is able and willing to fight for their submission ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/You%27ll_Be_Back_(song)" title="You'll Be Back (song)">You'll Be Back</a>").</p>
<p>The revolution is underway, and Hamilton, Burr, and their friends join the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">Continental Army</a>. As the army <a href="/wiki/New_York_and_New_Jersey_campaign" title="New York and New Jersey campaign">retreats from New York City</a>, General <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> realizes he needs help to win the war. Though Hamilton desires a command and to fight on the front lines, he recognizes the opportunity Washington offers him, and accepts a position as his <a href="/wiki/Aide-de-camp" title="Aide-de-camp">aide-de-camp</a> ("Right Hand Man").</p>
<p>In the winter of 1780, the men attend a ball given by <a href="/wiki/Philip_Schuyler" title="Philip Schuyler">Philip Schuyler</a>, and Hamilton sets his sights on the man's daughters ("A Winter's Ball"). Eliza falls instantly in love, and after being introduced by Angelica, Eliza and Hamilton soon wed ("<a href="/wiki/Helpless_(Hamilton_song)" title="Helpless (Hamilton song)">Helpless</a>"). Angelica is also smitten with Hamilton, but swallows her feelings for the sake of her sister's happiness ("<a href="/wiki/Satisfied_(Hamilton_song)" title="Satisfied (Hamilton song)">Satisfied</a>"). Hamilton, Laurens, Lafayette and Mulligan drunkenly celebrate the marriage when Burr arrives to offer congratulations. After Laurens teases him, Burr admits that he is having an affair with <a href="/wiki/Theodosia_Bartow_Prevost" title="Theodosia Bartow Prevost">Theodosia Bartow Prevost</a>, the wife of a British officer ("<a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_Tonight#Reprises" title="The Story of Tonight">The Story of Tonight (Reprise)</a>"). Hamilton urges Burr to make the relationship public. Burr, however, prefers to wait and see what life has in store for him rather than take any drastic measures ("<a href="/wiki/Wait_for_It_(song)" title="Wait for It (song)">Wait For It</a>").</p>
<p>As the revolution continues, Hamilton repeatedly petitions Washington to give him command, but Washington refuses, instead promoting <a href="/wiki/Charles_Lee_(general)" title="Charles Lee (general)">Charles Lee</a>. This decision proves disastrous at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Monmouth" title="Battle of Monmouth">Battle of Monmouth</a>, where Lee orders a retreat against Washington's orders, which prompts the commander to remove him from command in favor of Lafayette. Disgruntled, Lee spreads slanderous and vindictive rumors about Washington ("Stay Alive"). Hamilton is offended, but Washington orders Hamilton to ignore the comments. Hamilton does not wish to do so, but cannot disobey a direct order; instead, Laurens <a href="/wiki/Duel" title="Duel">duels</a> Lee, with Hamilton as his second, and Burr as Lee's second. Laurens is satisfied after he injures Lee and Lee yields ("<a href="/wiki/Ten_Duel_Commandments" title="Ten Duel Commandments">Ten Duel Commandments</a>"). Washington is angered by the duel, and orders Hamilton to return home to his wife ("Meet Me Inside"). When Hamilton returns home, Eliza tells him she is pregnant. She reassures a hesitant Hamilton that he doesn't need fame or fortune to live a happy life by her side ("That Would Be Enough").</p>
<p>Lafayette takes a larger leadership role in the revolution, persuading France to join the American cause, and the balance shifts in favor of the Continental Army. Washington and Lafayette realize they can win the war by <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Yorktown" title="Siege of Yorktown">cutting off the British navy at Yorktown</a>, but they will need Hamilton to do so, and the general offers him his long-desired command ("Guns and Ships"). On the eve of battle, Washington recalls his disastrous first command, and advises Hamilton that no man can control how he is remembered ("History Has Its Eyes on You"). After several days of fighting, the Continental Army is victorious. The British surrender in the last major battle of the war ("Yorktown (The World Turned Upside Down)"). His forces defeated, King George asks the rebels how they expect to successfully govern on their own ("What Comes Next?").</p>
<p>Soon after the victory at Yorktown, Hamilton's son <a href="/wiki/Philip_Hamilton" title="Philip Hamilton">Philip</a> is born, while Burr has a daughter, <a href="/wiki/Theodosia_Burr_Alston" title="Theodosia Burr Alston">Theodosia</a> ("<a href="/wiki/Dear_Theodosia" title="Dear Theodosia">Dear Theodosia</a>"). Hamilton receives word that Laurens has been killed in a seemingly pointless battle (the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Combahee_River" title="Battle of the Combahee River">Battle of the Combahee River</a>) and throws himself into his work. ("Tomorrow There'll Be More of Us").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominick_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dominick-14">[14]</a></sup> Hamilton and Burr both return to New York to finish their studies and pursue careers as lawyers. Burr is in awe of Hamilton's unyielding work ethic and becomes increasingly irritated by his success. Hamilton is chosen as a delegate to the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Convention_(United_States)" title="Constitutional Convention (United States)">Constitutional Convention</a> in the summer of 1787. Hamilton enlists <a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Jay" title="John Jay">John Jay</a> to write <i><a href="/wiki/The_Federalist_Papers" title="The Federalist Papers">The Federalist Papers</a></i> after Burr refuses. Angelica announces that she has found a husband and will be moving to London. The newly elected President Washington enlists Hamilton for the job of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Secretary of the Treasury">Treasury Secretary</a>, despite Eliza's protests ("Non-Stop").</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Act_Two">Act Two</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Act Two">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1789, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a> returns to the U.S. from France, where he spent most of the <a href="/wiki/Articles_of_Confederation" title="Articles of Confederation">Articles of Confederation</a> era as an ambassador. Immediately upon returning, he briefly addresses <a href="/wiki/Sally_Hemings" title="Sally Hemings">Sally Hemings</a>, asking her to open a letter from Washington, requesting that he become the first secretary of State under the new Constitution. Upon Jefferson's arrival in New York, <a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a> asks for Jefferson's help to stop <a href="/wiki/First_Report_on_the_Public_Credit" title="First Report on the Public Credit">Hamilton's financial plan</a>, which Madison believes gives the government too much control ("What'd I Miss?"). Jefferson and Hamilton debate the merits of Hamilton's financial plan during a <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_States" title="Cabinet of the United States">Cabinet</a> meeting. Washington pulls Hamilton aside, and tells him to figure out a compromise to win over Congress ("<a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Battle" title="Cabinet Battle">Cabinet Battle</a> #1").</p>
<p>While Hamilton is working at home, Eliza reminds him that <a href="/wiki/Philip_Hamilton" title="Philip Hamilton">Philip</a>, their son, is turning nine years old. Philip presents Hamilton with a short rap he composed, amazing his father. Angelica advises Hamilton to convince Jefferson of his plan so Congress will accept it. She also mentions a letter recently received from Hamilton, in which he referred to her as his "dearest," and wondering if it was intentional. Later, Eliza and Angelica try to persuade Hamilton to accompany them on vacation for the summer, but Hamilton refuses, saying that he has to work on his plan for Congress, staying in New York while the family goes upstate ("Take a Break").</p>
<p>While alone, Hamilton is visited by <a href="/wiki/Maria_Reynolds" title="Maria Reynolds">Maria Reynolds</a>, who claims she has been deserted by her husband. When Hamilton offers to help her, <a href="/wiki/Hamilton%E2%80%93Reynolds_sex_scandal" title="Hamilton–Reynolds sex scandal">they begin an affair</a>. Maria's husband James Reynolds blackmails Hamilton, who is furious with Maria but pays Reynolds and continues the affair ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Say_No_To_This" title="Say No To This">Say No To This</a>").</p>
<p>Hamilton discusses his plan with Jefferson and Madison over a private dinner, which results in the <a href="/wiki/Compromise_of_1790" title="Compromise of 1790">Compromise of 1790</a>, giving support to Hamilton's financial plan in exchange for <a href="/wiki/Residence_Act" title="Residence Act">moving the United States capital</a> from New York to Washington, D.C., a site much closer to Jefferson's home in Virginia. Burr is envious of Hamilton's sway in the government and wishes he had similar power ("<a href="/wiki/The_Room_Where_It_Happens" title="The Room Where It Happens">The Room Where It Happens</a>"). Burr switches political parties and defeats Eliza's father, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Schuyler" title="Philip Schuyler">Philip Schuyler</a>, in a race for Schuyler's seat in the Senate. This drives a wedge between Burr and Hamilton—the latter believes that Burr holds no loyalties and will stop at nothing to gain influence ("Schuyler Defeated").</p>
<p>In another Cabinet meeting, Jefferson and Hamilton argue over whether the United States should assist France in its <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_First_Coalition" title="War of the First Coalition">conflict with Britain</a>. Washington ultimately agrees with Hamilton's argument for remaining <a href="/wiki/Proclamation_of_Neutrality" title="Proclamation of Neutrality">neutral</a> ("Cabinet Battle #2"). After the meeting, Burr, Jefferson, and Madison share their envy of Washington's perennial support of Hamilton's policies. They begin to seek a way to damage Hamilton's public image ("Washington on Your Side").</p>
<p>Washington tells Hamilton that Jefferson has resigned from his position in order to run for president, and that Washington himself is stepping down. Hamilton is shocked, but Washington convinces him that it is the right thing to do, and they write a <a href="/wiki/George_Washington%27s_Farewell_Address" title="George Washington's Farewell Address">farewell address</a> ("<a href="/wiki/One_Last_Time_(Hamilton)" title="One Last Time (Hamilton)">One Last Time</a>"). In England, King George III receives word that Washington is stepping down and will be replaced with <a href="/wiki/John_Adams" title="John Adams">John Adams</a>. The king exits merrily, ready to enjoy the United States' suffering through the political turmoil caused by transitions in leadership, and Adams' inexperience ("I Know Him").</p>
<p>Hamilton is fired by Adams and publishes an inflammatory critique of the new president as a response ("The Adams Administration"). Jefferson, Madison and Burr believe they have found proof that Hamilton embezzled government money, effectively committing treason. When confronted, Hamilton admits to his affair with Maria Reynolds and his furtive payments to James Reynolds ("We Know"). Though the men swear to keep his secret, Burr reminds Hamilton that rumors grow, and Hamilton worries that the truth will get out. He reflects on how writing openly and honestly has saved him in the past ("Hurricane"), and publishes a public admission about the affair, hoping to snuff out rumors of embezzlement and save his political legacy. His personal reputation, however, is ruined following the publication of his <i><a href="/wiki/Hamilton%E2%80%93Reynolds_sex_scandal" title="Hamilton–Reynolds sex scandal">Observations</a></i> ("<a href="/wiki/The_Reynolds_Pamphlet_(song)" title="The Reynolds Pamphlet (song)">The Reynolds Pamphlet</a>"). Heartbroken by his infidelity, Eliza tearfully burns the letters Hamilton has written her over the years, destroying Hamilton's chance at being redeemed by "future historians" and keeping the world from knowing how she reacted by "erasing herself from the narrative" ("Burn").</p>
<p>Years pass, and Philip, now grown, challenges <a href="/wiki/George_Eacker" title="George Eacker">George Eacker</a> to a duel for insulting his father. Following Alexander's advice, Philip aims for the sky at the beginning of the duel, hoping the gesture would cause Eacker to stand down, but at the count of seven, Eacker shoots him ("Blow Us All Away"). Philip is taken to a doctor, who is unable to save him. Hamilton and Eliza separately arrive not long before Philip dies ("Stay Alive (Reprise)"). In the aftermath of Philip's death, the family moves uptown. Hamilton asks for Eliza's forgiveness for his mistakes, which he eventually receives ("<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Quiet_Uptown" title="It's Quiet Uptown">It's Quiet Uptown</a>").</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1800" title="United States presidential election, 1800">The presidential election of 1800</a> results in President John Adams' defeat, with Jefferson and Burr tied to win. Hamilton is upset that Burr holds no apparent principles, and so endorses Jefferson, who wins the presidency ("The Election of 1800"). Burr, angered, <a href="/wiki/Burr%E2%80%93Hamilton_duel" title="Burr–Hamilton duel">challenges Hamilton to a duel</a> via an exchange of letters ("<a href="/wiki/Your_Obedient_Servant_(song)" title="Your Obedient Servant (song)">Your Obedient Servant</a>"). Before sunrise on the morning of the duel, Eliza, unaware of the duel, asks Hamilton to come back to bed. Hamilton tells her he has an appointment, and tells her that he loves her ("Best of Wives and Best of Women").</p>
<p>Burr and Hamilton travel to <a href="/wiki/Weehawken,_New_Jersey" title="Weehawken, New Jersey">Weehawken, New Jersey</a> for the duel. Hamilton aims his pistol at the sky and is struck in the chest by Burr's bullet. Hamilton soliloquizes on death, his relationships, and his legacy. He dies soon after, with his wife and Angelica at his side. Burr laments that even though he survived, he is cursed to be the villain in history, remembered as the man who killed Alexander Hamilton ("<a href="/wiki/The_World_Was_Wide_Enough" title="The World Was Wide Enough">The World Was Wide Enough</a>").</p>
<p>The company congregates to close the story. Washington enters and reminds the audience that they have no control over how they will be remembered. Jefferson and Madison collectively admit the genius of their rival's financial plans. Eliza explains her role in preserving her husband's legacy over the next 50 years and frets that she has still not done enough. Addressing Hamilton directly, she tells him that she has established a private orphanage in his honor and she "can't wait to see [him] again" ("<a href="/wiki/Who_Lives,_Who_Dies,_Who_Tells_Your_Story" title="Who Lives, Who Dies, Who Tells Your Story">Who Lives, Who Dies, Who Tells Your Story</a>").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Roles_and_principal_casts">Roles and principal casts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Roles and principal casts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadway_cast_replacements">Broadway cast replacements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Broadway cast replacements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b>Alexander Hamilton:</b> <a href="/wiki/Javier_Mu%C3%B1oz_(actor)" title="Javier Muñoz (actor)">Javier Muñoz</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JavierMunozReplace_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-JavierMunozReplace-21">[21]</a></sup> Jevon McFerrin<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcferrin_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-mcferrin-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Alexander Hamilton <i>(Alternate)</i>:</b> Michael Luwoye; <a href="/wiki/Jon_Rua" title="Jon Rua">Jon Rua</a>; Jevon McFerrin</li>
<li><b>Eliza Hamilton:</b> Lexi Lawson<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lexhamilton_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-lexhamilton-23">[23]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Aaron Burr:</b> <a href="/wiki/Brandon_Victor_Dixon" title="Brandon Victor Dixon">Brandon Victor Dixon</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lexhamilton_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-lexhamilton-23">[23]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Breaker" title="Daniel Breaker">Daniel Breaker</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-24">[24]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Angelica Schuyler:</b> <a href="/wiki/Mandy_Gonzalez" title="Mandy Gonzalez">Mandy Gonzalez</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Marquis de Lafayette / Thomas Jefferson:</b> <a href="/wiki/Seth_Stewart" title="Seth Stewart">Seth Stewart</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Monroe_Iglehart" title="James Monroe Iglehart">James Monroe Iglehart</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>George Washington:</b> Nicholas Christopher;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Bryan Terrell Clark<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-majorcastchange_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-majorcastchange-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>King George III:</b> <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Rannells" title="Andrew Rannells">Andrew Rannells</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rory_O%27Malley" title="Rory O'Malley">Rory O'Malley</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snetiker_2016_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Snetiker_2016-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Taran_Killam" title="Taran Killam">Taran Killam</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-majorcastchange_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-majorcastchange-29">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brian_d%27Arcy_James" title="Brian d'Arcy James">Brian d'Arcy James</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Euan_Morton" title="Euan Morton">Euan Morton</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>John Laurens / Philip Hamilton:</b> <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Fisher" title="Jordan Fisher">Jordan Fisher</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Anthony Lee Medina<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-majorcastchange_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-majorcastchange-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Peggy Schuyler / Maria Reynolds:</b> Alysha Deslorieux<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-majorcastchange_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-majorcastchange-29">[29]</a></sup>; Joanna A. Jones</li>
<li><b>Hercules Mulligan / James Madison:</b> J. Quinton Johnson<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-majorcastchange_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-majorcastchange-29">[29]</a></sup></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_numbers">Musical numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Musical numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</dl>
<ul>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton_(song)" title="Alexander Hamilton (song)">Alexander Hamilton</a>" – Full company (except King George III)</li>
<li>"Aaron Burr, Sir" – Hamilton, Burr, Laurens, Lafayette, and Mulligan</li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/My_Shot" title="My Shot">My Shot</a>" – Hamilton, Laurens, Lafayette, Mulligan, Burr, Company</li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_Tonight" title="The Story of Tonight">The Story of Tonight</a>" – Hamilton, Laurens, Lafayette, and Mulligan</li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/The_Schuyler_Sisters" title="The Schuyler Sisters">The Schuyler Sisters</a>" – Angelica, Eliza, Peggy, Burr, and Company</li>
<li>"Farmer Refuted" – Samuel Seabury and Hamilton</li>
<li>"<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/You%27ll_Be_Back_(song)" title="You'll Be Back (song)">You'll Be Back</a>" – King George III</li>
<li>"Right Hand Man" – Washington, Hamilton, Burr, Laurens, Lafayette, Mulligan, and Company</li>
<li>"A Winter's Ball" – Burr, Hamilton, and Company men</li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/Helpless_(Hamilton_song)" title="Helpless (Hamilton song)">Helpless</a>" – Eliza, Hamilton, Angelica, and Company women</li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/Satisfied_(Hamilton_song)" title="Satisfied (Hamilton song)">Satisfied</a>" – Angelica, Eliza, Hamilton, and Company</li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_Tonight#Reprise" title="The Story of Tonight">The Story of Tonight</a>" (reprise) – Laurens, Lafayette, Mulligan, Hamilton, and Burr</li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/Wait_for_It_(song)" title="Wait for It (song)">Wait for It</a>" – Burr and Company</li>
<li>"Stay Alive" – Hamilton, Washington, Laurens, Lafayette, Mulligan, Eliza, Angelica, Lee, and Company</li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/Ten_Duel_Commandments" title="Ten Duel Commandments">Ten Duel Commandments</a>" – Laurens, Hamilton, Lee, Burr, and Company</li>
<li>"Meet Me Inside" – Washington, Hamilton, Burr, Laurens, and Company</li>
<li>"That Would Be Enough" – Eliza and Hamilton</li>
<li>"Guns and Ships" – Lafayette, Burr, Washington, and Company</li>
<li>"History Has Its Eyes on You" – Washington and Company</li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/Yorktown_(The_World_Turned_Upside_Down)" title="Yorktown (The World Turned Upside Down)">Yorktown (The World Turned Upside Down)</a>" – Hamilton, Lafayette, Laurens, Mulligan, Washington, and Company</li>
<li>"What Comes Next?" – King George III</li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/Dear_Theodosia" title="Dear Theodosia">Dear Theodosia</a>" – Burr and Hamilton</li>
<li>"Tomorrow There'll Be More of Us" – Laurens, (Eliza, Hamilton) †</li>
<li>"Non-Stop" – Hamilton, Burr, Eliza, Angelica, Washington, and Company</li>
</ul>
<p>† "<a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_Tonight" title="The Story of Tonight">Tomorrow There'll Be More of Us</a>", a second reprise to "<a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_Tonight" title="The Story of Tonight">The Story of Tonight</a>", is not included on the original Broadway cast recording. Miranda considers it "more of a scene rather than a song".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominick_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dominick-14">[14]</a></sup> It is the only scene not featured in the cast album.</p>
<p>‡ Previously titled "One Last Ride" in the Off-Broadway production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recordings">Recordings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Recordings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="Original_Broadway_cast_album_(2015)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Original_Broadway_cast_album_.282015.29">Original Broadway cast album (2015)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Original Broadway cast album (2015)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_(album)" title="Hamilton (album)">original Broadway cast recording for <i>Hamilton</i></a> was made available to listeners by <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a> on September 21, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> It was released by <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic Records</a> digitally on September 25, 2015, and physical copies were released on October 16, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The cast album has also been released on vinyl.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The album debuted at number 12 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> albums chart, the highest entrance for a cast recording since 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard-41">[41]</a></sup> It went on to reach number 3 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> and number 1 on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">Rap</a> albums chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rapchart_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-rapchart-43">[43]</a></sup> The original cast recording has won a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Musical_Theater_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Musical Theater Album">Grammy Award for Best Musical Theater Album</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grammy_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grammy-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span id="The_Hamilton_Mixtape_(2016)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Hamilton_Mixtape_.282016.29"><i>The Hamilton Mixtape</i> (2016)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The Hamilton Mixtape (2016)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Hamilton_Mixtape" title="The Hamilton Mixtape">The Hamilton Mixtape</a>,</i> a collection of remixes, covers, and samples of the musical's songs, was released on December 2, 2016. The <i>Mixtape</i> debuted in the number 1 spot on the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align: left"><img alt="" data-file-height="128" data-file-width="128" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Nuvola_apps_arts.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_arts.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Nuvola_apps_arts.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_arts.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Nuvola_apps_arts.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_arts.svg.png 2x" width="16"/> <a class="external text" href="http://www.npr.org/2016/04/09/473503407/lin-manuel-miranda-talks-hamilton-once-a-ridiculous-pitch-now-a-revolution" rel="nofollow">Lin-Manuel Miranda Talks 'Hamilton': Once A 'Ridiculous' Pitch, Now A Revolution</a>, interview with <a href="/wiki/Scott_Simon" title="Scott Simon">Scott Simon</a>, <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a>, April 9, 2016</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>While on vacation from performing in his hit <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a> show <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Heights" title="In the Heights">In the Heights</a></i>, Lin-Manuel Miranda bought a copy of <i>Alexander Hamilton</i> by <a href="/wiki/Ron_Chernow" title="Ron Chernow">Ron Chernow</a>, a biography of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton" title="Alexander Hamilton">Alexander Hamilton</a>, at an airport. After finishing the first few chapters, Miranda began to envision the life of Hamilton as a musical, and researched whether a stage musical of Hamilton's life had been created. All he found was that a <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_(play)" title="Hamilton (play)">play of Hamilton's story</a> had been done on Broadway in 1917, starring <a href="/wiki/George_Arliss" title="George Arliss">George Arliss</a> as Alexander Hamilton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>Miranda therefore began a project entitled <i>The Hamilton Mixtape.</i> On May 12, 2009, Miranda was invited to perform music from <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Heights" title="In the Heights">In the Heights</a></i> at the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> Evening of Poetry, Music and the Spoken Word. Instead, he performed the first song from <i>The Hamilton Mixtape</i>, a rough version of what would later become "Alexander Hamilton," <i>Hamilton</i>'s opening number. He spent a year after that working on "My Shot", another early number from the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-viagas_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-viagas-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>Miranda performed in a workshop production of the show, then titled <i>The Hamilton Mixtape</i>, at the <a href="/wiki/Vassar_College" title="Vassar College">Vassar</a> <a href="/wiki/Powerhouse_Theater" title="Powerhouse Theater">Reading Festival</a> on July 27, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The workshop production was directed by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Kail" title="Thomas Kail">Thomas Kail</a> and musically directed by <a href="/wiki/Alex_Lacamoire" title="Alex Lacamoire">Alex Lacamoire</a>. The workshop consisted of the entirety of the first act of the show and three songs from the second act. The workshop was accompanied by Lacamoire on the piano.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-viagas_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-viagas-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>Of the original workshop cast, only three principal cast members played in the Off-Broadway production: Miranda, <a href="/wiki/Daveed_Diggs" title="Daveed Diggs">Daveed Diggs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Jackson_(actor)" title="Christopher Jackson (actor)">Christopher Jackson</a>. Most of the original Off-Broadway cast moved to Broadway, except <a href="/wiki/Brian_d%27Arcy_James" title="Brian d'Arcy James">Brian d'Arcy James</a>, who was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Groff" title="Jonathan Groff">Jonathan Groff</a> as King George III.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Productions">Productions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Productions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hamilton_off-broadway_poster.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="438" data-file-width="227" height="424" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8d/Hamilton_off-broadway_poster.png/220px-Hamilton_off-broadway_poster.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/8d/Hamilton_off-broadway_poster.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hamilton_off-broadway_poster.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Off-Broadway promotional poster.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span id="Off-Broadway_(2015)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Off-Broadway_.282015.29">Off-Broadway (2015)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Off-Broadway (2015)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Directed by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Kail" title="Thomas Kail">Thomas Kail</a> and choreographed by <a href="/wiki/Andy_Blankenbuehler" title="Andy Blankenbuehler">Andy Blankenbuehler</a>, the musical received its world premiere <a href="/wiki/Off-Broadway" title="Off-Broadway">Off-Broadway</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_Public_Theater" title="The Public Theater">The Public Theater</a>, under the supervision of the Public's Artistic Director <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Eustis" title="Oskar Eustis">Oskar Eustis</a>, with previews starting on January 20, 2015 and officially opening on February 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTOBreview_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTOBreview-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gioia_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-gioia-51">[51]</a></sup> The production was extended twice, first to April 5 and then to May 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Chernow served as historical consultant to the production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mead_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-mead-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TPT-H_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-TPT-H-53">[53]</a></sup> The show opened to universal acclaim according to review aggregator <i>Did He Like It</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHLIOB_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-DHLIOB-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Broadway_(2015–present)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadway_.282015.E2.80.93present.29">Broadway (2015–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Broadway (2015–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Hamilton</i> premiered on Broadway at the <a href="/wiki/Richard_Rodgers_Theatre" title="Richard Rodgers Theatre">Richard Rodgers Theatre</a> (also home to Miranda's 2008 Broadway debut <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Heights" title="In the Heights">In the Heights</a></i>) on July 13, 2015 in previews, and opened on August 6, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brantley_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-brantley-1">[1]</a></sup> The production is produced by <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Seller" title="Jeffrey Seller">Jeffrey Seller</a> and features scenic design by David Korins, costumes by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tazewell" title="Paul Tazewell">Paul Tazewell</a>, lighting by <a href="/wiki/Howell_Binkley" title="Howell Binkley">Howell Binkley</a> and sound by Nevin Steinberg, who all reprised their roles from the off-Broadway production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The production was critically acclaimed by many theater analysts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brantley_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-brantley-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Chicago_(2016–present)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Chicago_.282016.E2.80.93present.29">Chicago (2016–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Chicago (2016–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Hamilton</i> opened at the <a href="/wiki/CIBC_Theatre" title="CIBC Theatre">CIBC Theatre</a> in Chicago on October 19, 2016, following previews from September 27, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> It is currently booking through April 29, 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> According to lead producer <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Seller" title="Jeffrey Seller">Jeffrey Seller</a>, the show may be in residence for two years or more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> On its opening, attended by author Miranda, the Chicago production received strongly positive reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Miranda praised the Chicago casts' performance during a later television interview.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="U.S._touring_productions_(2017)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._touring_productions_.282017.29">U.S. touring productions (2017)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: U.S. touring productions (2017)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Plans for a national tour of <i>Hamilton</i> emerged near the end of January 2016. The tour was initially announced with over 20 stops, scheduled from 2017 through at least 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vankin_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vankin-65">[65]</a></sup> Tickets to the tour's run in San Francisco—its debut city—sold out within 24 hours of release; the number of people who entered the online waiting room to purchase tickets surpassed 110,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The first national touring production began preview performances at San Francisco's <a href="/wiki/Orpheum_Theatre_(San_Francisco)" title="Orpheum Theatre (San Francisco)">SHN Orpheum Theatre</a> on March 10, 2017 and officially opened on March 23. The production ran in San Francisco until August 5, when it transferred to Los Angeles' <a href="/wiki/Pantages_Theatre_(Hollywood)" title="Pantages Theatre (Hollywood)">Hollywood Pantages Theatre</a> for a run from August 11 to December 30, 2017.</p>
<p>Just days after the first U.S. tour began performances in San Francisco, news emerged that a second U.S. tour of <i>Hamilton</i> would begin in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> for a six-week limited engagement before touring North America concurrently with the first tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Desk_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Desk-11">[11]</a></sup> To distinguish the first and second touring productions, the production team has labeled them, respectively, the "Angelica tour" and the "Philip tour."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vankin_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vankin-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Angelica tour alone requires 14 truckloads of cargo and a core group of over 60 traveling cast, crew, and musicians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vankin_65-2"><a href="#cite_note-Vankin-65">[65]</a></sup> The production team insisted that each tour must be able to duplicate the original Broadway show's choreography, which literally revolves around two concentric turntables on the stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vankin_65-3"><a href="#cite_note-Vankin-65">[65]</a></sup> This led to the construction of four portable sets, two for each tour, so that one set can be assembled well in advance at the next stop while the tour is still playing at the last stop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vankin_65-4"><a href="#cite_note-Vankin-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="West_End_(2017)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="West_End_.282017.29">West End (2017)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: West End (2017)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cameron_Mackintosh" title="Cameron Mackintosh">Cameron Mackintosh</a> will produce a London production which will re-open the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Palace_Theatre" title="Victoria Palace Theatre">Victoria Palace Theatre</a> (currently undergoing a refurbishment following the closure of <i><a href="/wiki/Billy_Elliot_the_Musical" title="Billy Elliot the Musical">Billy Elliot the Musical</a></i>) on December 21, 2017, following previews from December 6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-10">[10]</a></sup> Initial principal casting was announced on January 26, 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-broadway.com_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-broadway.com-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office_and_business">Box office and business</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Box office and business">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The musical's engagement at the Off-Broadway Public Theater was sold out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Revolutionary_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Revolutionary-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>When the musical opened on Broadway, it had a multimillion-dollar advance in ticket sales, reportedly taking in $30 million before its official opening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> <i>Hamilton</i> was the second-highest-grossing show on Broadway for the Labor Day week ending September 6, 2015 (behind only <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_(musical)" title="The Lion King (musical)">The Lion King</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> As of September 2015, the show has been sold out for most of its Broadway engagement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoxOffice1_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-BoxOffice1-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Hamilton</i>, like other Broadway musicals, offers a lottery before every show. Twenty-one front row seats and occasional standing room are given out in the lottery. Chosen winners are able to purchase two tickets at $10 each. Unlike other Broadway shows, <i>Hamilton</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s lottery process drew in large crowds of people that created a significant congestion problems for West 46th Street.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Even though many people were not able to win the lottery, <i>Hamilton</i> creator Lin-Manuel Miranda prepared mini-performances, right before the lotteries were drawn. They were dubbed the '#Ham4Ham' shows, due to the fact that if you won, you gave a Hamilton (a $10 bill) in exchange for seeing the show. People were then able to experience a part of the show even when they did not win the lottery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The lottery was eventually placed online to avoid increasing crowds and dangerous traffic conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> On its first day, more than 50,000 people entered, which resulted in the website crashing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Trevor Boffone<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (May 2017)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> in his essay on <a href="/wiki/HowlRound" title="HowlRound">HowlRound</a> wrote: "Ham4Ham follows a long tradition of Latina/o (or the ancestors of present-day Latina/os) theatremaking that dates back to when the events in <i>Hamilton</i> were happening. (...) The philosophy behind this is simple. If the people won't come to the theatre, then take the theatre to the people. While <a href="/wiki/Teatro_Campesino" title="Teatro Campesino">El Teatro Campesino</a>'s 'taking it to the streets' originated from a place of social protest, Ham4Ham does so to create accessibility, tap into social media, and ultimately generate a free, self-functioning marketing campaign. In this way, Ham4Ham falls into a lineage of accessibility as a Latina/o theatremaking aesthetic."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Following Miranda's departure from the show on July 9, 2016, Rory O'Malley, then playing King George III, took over as the host of Ham4Ham.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The Ham4Ham show officially ended on August 31, 2016, after over a year of performances, though the lottery still continues daily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Hamilton</i> set a Broadway box office record for the most money grossed in a single week in New York City. In late November 2016, it grossed $3.3 million for an eight performance week, the first show to break $3 million in eight performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_response">Critical response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Critical response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Marilyn Stasio, in her review of the Off-Broadway production for <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i>, wrote, "The music is exhilarating, but the lyrics are the big surprise. The sense as well as the sound of the sung dialogue has been purposely suited to each character. George Washington, a stately figure in Jackson's dignified performance, sings in polished prose... But in the end, Miranda's impassioned narrative of one man's story becomes the collective narrative of a nation, a nation built by immigrants who occasionally need to be reminded where they came from."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Obama_greets_the_cast_and_crew_of_Hamilton_musical,_2015.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1333" data-file-width="2000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Obama_greets_the_cast_and_crew_of_Hamilton_musical%2C_2015.jpg/220px-Obama_greets_the_cast_and_crew_of_Hamilton_musical%2C_2015.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Obama_greets_the_cast_and_crew_of_Hamilton_musical%2C_2015.jpg/330px-Obama_greets_the_cast_and_crew_of_Hamilton_musical%2C_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Obama_greets_the_cast_and_crew_of_Hamilton_musical%2C_2015.jpg/440px-Obama_greets_the_cast_and_crew_of_Hamilton_musical%2C_2015.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Obama_greets_the_cast_and_crew_of_Hamilton_musical,_2015.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i>Hamilton</i> cast and crew greets President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> on July 18, 2015.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In his review of the Off-Broadway production, Jesse Green in <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i> wrote, "The conflict between independence and interdependence is not just the show's subject but also its method: It brings the complexity of forming a union from disparate constituencies right to your ears.... Few are the theatergoers who will be familiar with all of Miranda's touchstones. I caught the verbal references to <a href="/wiki/Rodgers_and_Hammerstein" title="Rodgers and Hammerstein">Rodgers and Hammerstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_and_Sullivan" title="Gilbert and Sullivan">Gilbert and Sullivan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Sondheim" title="Stephen Sondheim">Sondheim</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/West_Side_Story" title="West Side Story">West Side Story</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/1776_(musical)" title="1776 (musical)">1776</a></i>, but other people had to point out to me the frequent hat-tips to hip-hop... Whether it's a watershed, a breakthrough, and a game changer, as some have been saying, is another matter. Miranda is too savvy (and loves his antecedents too much) to try to reinvent all the rules at once.... Those duels, by the way—there are three of them—are superbly handled, the highlights of a riveting if at times overbusy staging by the director Thomas Kail and the choreographer Andy Blankenbuehler."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Although giving a positive review, Elisabeth Vincentelli, of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_New_York_Post" title="The New York Post">The New York Post</a></i> (which was founded by Hamilton himself), wrote that Hamilton and Burr's love/hate relationship "fails to drive the show—partly because Miranda lacks the charisma and intensity of the man he portrays," and that "too many of the numbers are exposition-heavy lessons, as if this were 'Schoolhouse Rap!' The show is burdened with eye-glazingly dull stretches, especially those involving George Washington."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ben_Brantley" title="Ben Brantley">Ben Brantley</a> in reviewing the Broadway production in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, wrote, "I am loath to tell people to mortgage their houses and lease their children to acquire tickets to a hit Broadway show. But <i>Hamilton</i>, directed by Thomas Kail and starring Mr. Miranda, might just about be worth it.... Washington, Jefferson, Madison—they're all here, making war and writing constitutions and debating points of economic structure. So are Aaron Burr and the Marquis de Lafayette. They wear the clothes (by Paul Tazewell) you might expect them to wear in a traditional costume drama, and the big stage they inhabit has been done up (by David Korins) to suggest a period-appropriate tavern, where incendiary youth might gather to drink, brawl and plot revolution."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brantley_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-brantley-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/David_Cote_(writer)" title="David Cote (writer)">David Cote</a> in his review of the Broadway production for <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time_Out_New_York" title="Time Out New York">Time Out New York</a></i> wrote, "I love <i>Hamilton</i>. I love it like I love New York, or Broadway when it gets it right. And this is so right... A sublime conjunction of radio-ready hip-hop (as well as R&amp;B, Britpop and trad showstoppers), under-dramatized American history and Miranda's uniquely personal focus as a first-generation Puerto Rican and inexhaustible wordsmith, Hamilton hits multilevel culture buttons, hard... The work's human drama and novelistic density remain astonishing." He chose <i>Hamilton</i> as a Critics' Pick, and gave the production five out of five stars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cote_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cote-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>A review in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> notes that the production enjoys "near-universal critical acclaim".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Economist2015_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Economist2015-80">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> joked that admiration for the musical is "the only thing <a href="/wiki/Dick_Cheney" title="Dick Cheney">Dick Cheney</a> and I agree on."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honors_and_awards">Honors and awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_(musical)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Honors and awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>‡ Blankenbuehler received a Special <a href="/wiki/Drama_Desk_Award" title="Drama Desk Award">Drama Desk Award</a> for "his inspired and heart-stopping choreography in <i>Hamilton</i>, which is indispensible [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>] to the musical's storytelling. His body of work is versatile, yet a dynamic and fluid style is consistently evident. When it's time to 'take his shot,' Blankenbuehler hits the bull's-eye."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DDesk_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-DDesk-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
